it...","image":["https://cdn.sanity.io/images/fo9xc2x1/production/67df7b3a4e3e492afebc71b146b2e75763e9dbb4-3600x1690.png?rect=298,0,3004,1690&w=1920&h=1080&fm=webp&q=80&fit=max&auto=format&dpr=2"],"publisher":{"@type":"Organization","name":"Website"},"datePublished":"2021-03-11T18:00:00.000Z","dateModified":"2025-08-20T14:04:44.000Z","url":"https://www.intel471.comyou-dont-know-the-hafnium-of-it","mainEntityOfPage":{"@type":"WebPage","@id":"https://www.intel471.comyou-dont-know-the-hafnium-of-it"}}</script><section class="mx-auto" data-sanity="id=guAE65hUAdLkqFEqZeyMYn;type=blog;path=pageBuilder;base=https%3A%2F%2Fintel471.sanity.studio"><div data-sanity="id=guAE65hUAdLkqFEqZeyMYn;type=blog;path=pageBuilder:ZwZKqsE7GiWU;base=https%3A%2F%2Fintel471.sanity.studio"><section class="relative container bg-white lg:pt-12 xl:pt-16 pb-8 md:pb-10 lg:pb-12 xl:pb-16 pt-12 md:pt-[56px]"><div class="max-w-4xl mx-auto"><div class="max-w-none rich-text"><h3 id="if-you-want-to-get-access-to-cyborg-securitys-community-defense-measures-for-the-hafnium-attack-including-our-free-detection-content-click-here-or-scroll-down-to-the-detection-content-section-keep-reading-for-an-overview-of-the-attack-and-what-we-know-so-far" class="scroll-m-20 h3"><strong>If you want to get access to Cyborg Security&#x27;s Community Defense Measures for the HAFNIUM attack, including our free detection content, click <a class="underline decoration-2 decoration-red-600 underline-offset-2 break-words hover:decoration-red-700" aria-label="Link to #9" target="_blank" href="#9">here</a> or scroll down to the &quot;Detection Content&quot; section! Keep reading for an overview of the attack and what we know so far!</strong></h3><p> After little more than a month of reprieve, the infosec community is, once again, back into it. This time the target, though, is even more prevalent than SolarWinds&#x27; Orion. Now the target is Microsoft&#x27;s Exchange, and the exploited vulnerability allows for remote code execution (or RCE). We&#x27;ve distilled down the facts of the HAFNIUM attack to answer the most important questions.</p><p><strong>Table of Contents</strong></p><ol class="list-decimal list-inside space-y-2 my-4 ml-4 xl:ml-6"><li class=""><a class="underline decoration-2 decoration-red-600 underline-offset-2 break-words hover:decoration-red-700" aria-label="Link to #1" target="_blank" href="#1">What We Know So Far about HAFNIUM</a></li><li class=""><a class="underline decoration-2 decoration-red-600 underline-offset-2 break-words hover:decoration-red-700" aria-label="Link to #2" target="_blank" href="#2">Who Are They?</a></li><li class=""><a class="underline decoration-2 decoration-red-600 underline-offset-2 break-words hover:decoration-red-700" aria-label="Link to #3" target="_blank" href="#3">Where is HAFNIUM From?</a></li><li class=""><a class="underline decoration-2 decoration-red-600 underline-offset-2 break-words hover:decoration-red-700" aria-label="Link to #4" target="_blank" href="#4">Who is Being Targeted?</a></li><li class=""><a class="underline decoration-2 decoration-red-600 underline-offset-2 break-words hover:decoration-red-700" aria-label="Link to #5" target="_blank" href="#5">What Are The Actors Doing?</a></li><li class=""><a class="underline decoration-2 decoration-red-600 underline-offset-2 break-words hover:decoration-red-700" aria-label="Link to #6" target="_blank" href="#6">HAFNIUM MITRE ATT&amp;CK Techniques</a></li><li class=""><a class="underline decoration-2 decoration-red-600 underline-offset-2 break-words hover:decoration-red-700" aria-label="Link to #7" target="_blank" href="#7">When Did All This Happen?</a></li><li class=""><a class="underline decoration-2 decoration-red-600 underline-offset-2 break-words hover:decoration-red-700" aria-label="Link to #8" target="_blank" href="#8">What Should I Do?</a></li><li class=""><a class="underline decoration-2 decoration-red-600 underline-offset-2 break-words hover:decoration-red-700" aria-label="Link to #9" target="_blank" href="#9">Detection Content</a></li></ol><p> </p><h3 id="what-we-know-so-far-about-hafnium" class="scroll-m-20 h3"><strong>What We Know So Far about HAFNIUM</strong></h3><p> </p><p><strong>Who Are They?</strong></p><p>On 2 March 2021, Microsoft released a <a class="underline decoration-2 decoration-red-600 underline-offset-2 break-words hover:decoration-red-700" aria-label="Link to https://www.microsoft.com/security/blog/2021/03/02/hafnium-targeting-exchange-servers/#scan-log" target="_blank" href="https://www.microsoft.com/security/blog/2021/03/02/hafnium-targeting-exchange-servers/#scan-log">blog</a> article detailing a new threat actor it had dubbed <strong>HAFNIUM</strong>. Microsoft, the blog identified, has observed the actor exploiting several 0-day vulnerabilities.</p><p>Microsoft also highlighted that the HAFNIUM group had previously targeted other organizations. The group, Microsoft identified, has focused on the exploitation of Internet-facing services in the past.</p><p>Later that same day, the company Volexity also released a <a class="underline decoration-2 decoration-red-600 underline-offset-2 break-words hover:decoration-red-700" aria-label="Link to https://www.volexity.com/blog/2021/03/02/active-exploitation-of-microsoft-exchange-zero-day-vulnerabilities/" target="_blank" href="https://www.volexity.com/blog/2021/03/02/active-exploitation-of-microsoft-exchange-zero-day-vulnerabilities/">blog</a> article. In their article, they identified that they observed the attacks beginning as early as 3 January 2021.</p><p>Hot on the heels of the Microsoft and Volexity blogs, other vendors began to contribute information. On 4 March 2021, FireEye&#x27;s Mandiant Intelligence release their own <a class="underline decoration-2 decoration-red-600 underline-offset-2 break-words hover:decoration-red-700" aria-label="Link to https://www.fireeye.com/blog/threat-research/2021/03/detection-response-to-exploitation-of-microsoft-exchange-zero-day-vulnerabilities.html" target="_blank" href="https://www.fireeye.com/blog/threat-research/2021/03/detection-response-to-exploitation-of-microsoft-exchange-zero-day-vulnerabilities.html">blog</a> post. In it, FireEye identified that they tracked the activity under three separate activity clusters:</p><ul class="list-disc list-inside space-y-2 my-4 ml-4 xl:ml-6"><li class="">UNC2639</li><li class="">UNC2640</li><li class="">UNC2643</li></ul><p>One particularly important point in this blog article is that FireEye detected this activity all the way back in January 2021. The article also highlighted various TTPs and tools the actors used. This included:</p><ul class="list-disc list-inside space-y-2 my-4 ml-4 xl:ml-6"><li class="">ASPXSPY</li><li class="">Covenant</li><li class="">China Chopper</li><li class="">Nishang</li><li class="">PowerCat</li><li class="">Cobalt Strike</li></ul><p>They also described the actors&#x27; method of deploying webshells on compromised Exchange servers. These webshells were unique though. The webshells detected the presence of specific security products and warn the actors. The security products it detected included FireEye, Carbon Black and Crowdstrike. They described the actors technique of dropping more complex webshells over time. This appears to be to avoid detection.</p><p>In time, other vendors have also come forward, including <a class="underline decoration-2 decoration-red-600 underline-offset-2 break-words hover:decoration-red-700" aria-label="Link to https://symantec-enterprise-blogs.security.com/blogs/threat-intelligence/microsoft-exchange-server-protection" target="_blank" href="https://symantec-enterprise-blogs.security.com/blogs/threat-intelligence/microsoft-exchange-server-protection">Symantec</a>. They identified that they track HAFNIUM, under the name <strong>Ant</strong>.</p><p> </p><p><strong>Where is HAFNIUM From?</strong></p><p>Attribution can be a tricky topic in cyber threat intelligence. Despite this fact, <a class="underline decoration-2 decoration-red-600 underline-offset-2 break-words hover:decoration-red-700" aria-label="Link to https://www.forbes.com/sites/daveywinder/2021/03/04/microsoft-exchange-attacks-are-declared-an-emergency-by-homeland-security/" target="_blank" href="https://www.forbes.com/sites/daveywinder/2021/03/04/microsoft-exchange-attacks-are-declared-an-emergency-by-homeland-security/">several</a> <a class="underline decoration-2 decoration-red-600 underline-offset-2 break-words hover:decoration-red-700" aria-label="Link to https://www.washingtonpost.com/business/on-small-business/microsoft-attack-blamed-on-china-morphs-into-global-crisis/2021/03/06/48bffec4-7ee1-11eb-8c5e-32e47b42b51b_story.html" target="_blank" href="https://www.washingtonpost.com/business/on-small-business/microsoft-attack-blamed-on-china-morphs-into-global-crisis/2021/03/06/48bffec4-7ee1-11eb-8c5e-32e47b42b51b_story.html">sources</a>, including <a class="underline decoration-2 decoration-red-600 underline-offset-2 break-words hover:decoration-red-700" aria-label="Link to https://www.microsoft.com/security/blog/2021/03/02/hafnium-targeting-exchange-servers/" target="_blank" href="https://www.microsoft.com/security/blog/2021/03/02/hafnium-targeting-exchange-servers/">Microsoft</a>, have indicated that the HAFNIUM group is &quot;... state-sponsored and operating out of China ...&quot;</p><p> </p><p><strong>Who is Being Targeted?</strong></p><p>At this point, the targeting of HAFNIUM appears opportunistic. Indeed, since Microsoft released their initial blog, the actors <a class="underline decoration-2 decoration-red-600 underline-offset-2 break-words hover:decoration-red-700" aria-label="Link to https://krebsonsecurity.com/2021/03/at-least-30000-u-s-organizations-newly-hacked-via-holes-in-microsofts-email-software/" target="_blank" href="https://krebsonsecurity.com/2021/03/at-least-30000-u-s-organizations-newly-hacked-via-holes-in-microsofts-email-software/">have</a> &quot;... stepped up attacks on any vulnerable, unpatched Exchange servers (2013, 2016, and 2019) worldwide.&quot; The HAFNIUM group, though, has targeted organizations in the past.</p><p>As both Microsoft and FireEye mentioned, HAFNIUM is a group with a bit of track record. Microsoft identified that they have targeted several industries in the past. These included</p><ul class="list-disc list-inside space-y-2 my-4 ml-4 xl:ml-6"><li class="">Infectious disease research</li><li class="">Law firms</li><li class="">Universities</li><li class="">Defense contractors</li><li class="">Think tanks</li><li class="">Non-Governmental Organizations (NGOs)</li></ul><p>FireEye also mentioned that they had observed several industries affected by the new attack, including</p><ul class="list-disc list-inside space-y-2 my-4 ml-4 xl:ml-6"><li class="">Retailers</li><li class="">Local Governments</li><li class="">Universities</li><li class="">Engineering Firms</li></ul><p>They also identified that there is possible related activity observed in Asia as well</p><ul class="list-disc list-inside space-y-2 my-4 ml-4 xl:ml-6"><li class="">Federal governments</li><li class="">Telecommunications providers</li></ul><p> </p><p><strong>What Are The Actors Doing?</strong></p><p>Since early January, the actors have been exploiting several 0-day vulnerabilities in Exchange. The vulnerabilities, which affect on-premise versions of Microsoft Exchange only, are:</p><ul class="list-disc list-inside space-y-2 my-4 ml-4 xl:ml-6"><li class="">CVE-2021-26855</li><li class="">CVE-2021-26857</li><li class="">CVE-2021-26858</li><li class="">CVE-2021-27065</li></ul><p>Once the actors establish a foothold in the environment, they will deploy one or more web shells. These are small bits of code that gives the actors control over the system. Once in the environment, the actors use a variety of techniques.</p><p> </p><p><strong>HAFNIUM MITRE ATT&amp;CK Techniques</strong></p><p>T1003.001 - OS Credential Dumping: LSASS Memory</p><p>T1059.001 - Command and Scripting Interpreter: PowerShell</p><p>T1114.001 - Email Collection: Local Email Collection</p><p>T1136 - Create Account</p><p>T1003.003 - OS Credential Dumping: NTDS</p><p>T1021.002 - Remote Services: SMB/Windows Admin Shares</p><p>T1005 - Data from Local System</p><p>T1027 - Obfuscated Files or Information</p><p>T1046 - Network Service Scanning</p><p>T1059 - Command and Scripting Interpreter</p><p>T1070 - Indicator Removal on Host</p><p>T1071 - Application Layer Protocol</p><p>T1074.002 - Data Staged: Remote Data Staging</p><p>T1083 - File and Directory Discovery</p><p>T1110 - Brute Force</p><p>T1190 - Exploit Public-Facing Application</p><p>T1505 - Server Software Component</p><p>T1560.001 - Archive Collected Data: Archive via Utility</p><p>T1589.002 - Gather Victim Identity Information: Email Addresses</p><p>T1590.002 - Gather Victim Network Information: DNS</p><p> </p><p><strong>When Did All This Happen?</strong></p><p>Reporting from both <a class="underline decoration-2 decoration-red-600 underline-offset-2 break-words hover:decoration-red-700" aria-label="Link to https://www.fireeye.com/blog/threat-research/2021/03/detection-response-to-exploitation-of-microsoft-exchange-zero-day-vulnerabilities.html" target="_blank" href="https://www.fireeye.com/blog/threat-research/2021/03/detection-response-to-exploitation-of-microsoft-exchange-zero-day-vulnerabilities.html">FireEye</a> and <a class="underline decoration-2 decoration-red-600 underline-offset-2 break-words hover:decoration-red-700" aria-label="Link to https://www.volexity.com/blog/2021/03/02/active-exploitation-of-microsoft-exchange-zero-day-vulnerabilities/" target="_blank" href="https://www.volexity.com/blog/2021/03/02/active-exploitation-of-microsoft-exchange-zero-day-vulnerabilities/">Volexity</a> state that the attacks were first observed in January. It is unknown whether this was the start of the campaign.</p><p>The bulk of the campaign appears to have taken place over February and March 2021.</p><p> </p><p><strong>What Should I Do?</strong></p><p>What you should do next will likely depend on a few factors.</p><ul class="list-disc list-inside space-y-2 my-4 ml-4 xl:ml-6"><li class="">Cyborg Security has <a class="underline decoration-2 decoration-red-600 underline-offset-2 break-words hover:decoration-red-700" aria-label="Link to https://cta-redirect.hubspot.com/cta/redirect/7924572/c4f6d0f6-bbce-4628-bc69-6e1f29ae348e" target="_blank" href="https://cta-redirect.hubspot.com/cta/redirect/7924572/c4f6d0f6-bbce-4628-bc69-6e1f29ae348e">released new advanced detection</a> content through its Community Defense Measures (CDM) project. This content will alert organization to malicious behaviors related to the attacks.</li><li class="">Microsoft <a class="underline decoration-2 decoration-red-600 underline-offset-2 break-words hover:decoration-red-700" aria-label="Link to https://github.com/microsoft/CSS-Exchange/tree/main/Security" target="_blank" href="https://github.com/microsoft/CSS-Exchange/tree/main/Security">has released</a> a tool that will scan Exchange logs for suspicious and malicious modifications.</li><li class="">Microsoft has also released <a class="underline decoration-2 decoration-red-600 underline-offset-2 break-words hover:decoration-red-700" aria-label="Link to https://msrc-blog.microsoft.com/2021/03/02/multiple-security-updates-released-for-exchange-server/" target="_blank" href="https://msrc-blog.microsoft.com/2021/03/02/multiple-security-updates-released-for-exchange-server/">security updates</a> for Microsoft Exchange</li><li class="">The Cybersecurity and Infrastructure Security Agency (CISA) has also released <a class="underline decoration-2 decoration-red-600 underline-offset-2 break-words hover:decoration-red-700" aria-label="Link to https://us-cert.cisa.gov/ncas/alerts/aa21-062a" target="_blank" href="https://us-cert.cisa.gov/ncas/alerts/aa21-062a">Alert AA21-062A</a>. An important note about this is that CISA warns organizations: &quot;... [if] your organization [sees] evidence of compromise, your incident response should begin with conducting forensic analysis to collect artifacts and perform triage ....&quot;</li><li class="">The US&#x27; Department of Homeland Security also issued <a class="underline decoration-2 decoration-red-600 underline-offset-2 break-words hover:decoration-red-700" aria-label="Link to https://cyber.dhs.gov/ed/21-02/" target="_blank" href="https://cyber.dhs.gov/ed/21-02/">Emergency Directive 21-02</a>.</li></ul><p><strong>Detection Content</strong></p><p><strong>To get Cyborg Security&#x27;s HAFNIUM Community Defense Measures, click the button below. No sign up required!</strong></p><p>[Image: FREE DETECTION CONTENT]</p></div></div></section></div></section></main><section class="bg-neutral-50 pt-8 pb-12 md:pt-12 md:pb-16"><div underline-offset-2 decoration-transparent">CrazyHunter Ransomware</h3><p class="text-sm mt-3 text-neutral-700 line-clamp-4">CrazyHunter is a ransomware campaign targeting healthcare that weakens endpoint defenses and escalates privileges before encrypting systems at scale.</p></div></article></a><a class="group block h-full" href="/blog/devman-ransomware"><article class="flex flex-col h-full bg-white overflow-hidden"><div class="relative w-full aspect-[4/3] overflow-hidden bg-gray-100"><div class="h-full w-full transform transition-all duration-500 group-hover:scale-105"><img alt="Intel 471 Logo 2024.png" aria-label="DevMan Ransomware" loading="lazy" width="600" height="450" decoding="async" data-nimg="1" class="w-full h-full object-cover" style="color:transparent" sizes="(max-width: 640px) 75vw, (max-width: 768px) 50vw, (max-width: 1200px) 33vw, 25vw"
